     173                 :            : /*
     174                 :            :  * create_plan
     175                 :            :  *        Creates the access plan for a query by tracing backwards through the
     176                 :            :  *        desired chain of pathnodes, starting at the node 'best_path'.  For
     177                 :            :  *        every pathnode found, we create a corresponding plan node containing
     178                 :            :  *        appropriate id, target list, and qualification information.
     179                 :            :  *
     180                 :            :  *        The tlists and quals in the plan tree are still in planner format,
     181                 :            :  *        ie, Vars still correspond to the parser's numbering.  This will be
     182                 :            :  *        fixed later by setrefs.c.
     183                 :            :  *
     184                 :            :  *        best_path is the best access path
     185                 :            :  *

     568                 :            : /*
     569                 :            :  * create_gating_plan
     570                 :            :  *        Deal with pseudoconstant qual clauses
     571                 :            :  *
     572                 :            :  * If the node's quals list includes any pseudoconstant quals, put them
     573                 :            :  * into a gating Result node atop the already-built plan.  Otherwise,
     574                 :            :  * return the plan as-is.
     575                 :            :  *
     576                 :            :  * Note that we don't change cost or size estimates when doing gating.
     577                 :            :  * The costs of qual eval were already folded into the plan's startup cost.
     578                 :            :  * Leaving the size alone amounts to assuming that the gating qual will
     579                 :            :  * succeed, which is the conservative estimate for planning upper queries.
     580                 :            :  * We certainly don't want to assume the output size is zero (unless the
     581                 :            :  * gating qual is actually constant FALSE, and that case is dealt with in
     582                 :            :  * clausesel.c).  Interpolating between the two cases is silly, because
     583                 :            :  * it doesn't reflect what will really happen at runtime, and besides which
     584                 :            :  * in most cases we have only a very bad idea of the probability of the gating
     585                 :            :  * qual being true.
     586                 :            :  */

     602                 :          0 :                                                                 plan->targetlist,
     603                 :          0 :                                                                 (Node *) pseudoconstants,
     604                 :          0 :                                                                 plan);
     605                 :          0 : }

     839         [ #  # ]:          0 :         if (best_path->umethod == UNIQUE_PATH_LIMIT1)

     857                 :            :         /*----------
     858                 :            :          * As constructed, the subplan has a "flat" tlist containing just the
     859                 :            :          * Vars needed here and at upper levels.  The values we are supposed
     860                 :            :          * to unique-ify may be expressions in these variables.  We have to
     861                 :            :          * add any such expressions to the subplan's tlist.
     862                 :            :          *
     863                 :            :          * The subplan may have a "physical" tlist if it is a simple scan plan.
     864                 :            :          * If we're going to sort, this should be reduced to the regular tlist,
     865                 :            :          * so that we don't sort more data than we need to.  For hashing, the
     866                 :            :          * tlist should be left as-is if we don't need to add any expressions;
     867                 :            :          * but if we do have to add expressions, then a projection step will be
     868                 :            :          * needed at runtime anyway, so we may as well remove unneeded items.
     869                 :            :          * Therefore newtlist starts from build_relation_tlist() not just a
     870                 :            :          * copy of the subplan's tlist; and we don't install it into the subplan
     871                 :            :          * unless we are sorting or stuff has to be added.
     872                 :            :          *
     873                 :            :          * To find the correct list of values to unique-ify, we look in the
     874                 :            :          * information saved for IN expressions.  If this code is ever used in
     875                 :            :          * other scenarios, some other way of finding what to unique-ify will
     876                 :            :          * be needed.  The IN clause's operators are needed too, since they
     877                 :            :          * determine what the meaning of "unique" is in this context.
     878                 :            :          *----------
     879                 :            :          */

    1163                 :            : /*
    1164                 :            :  * create_externalscan_plan
    1165                 :            :  *       Returns an externalscan plan for the base relation scanned by 'best_path'
    1166                 :            :  *       with restriction clauses 'scan_clauses' and targetlist 'tlist'.
    1167                 :            :  *
    1168                 :            :  *       The external plan also includes the data format specification and file
    1169                 :            :  *       location specification. Here is where we do the mapping of external file
    1170                 :            :  *       to segment database and add it to the plan (or bail out of the mapping
    1171                 :            :  *       rules are broken)
    1172                 :            :  *
    1173                 :            :  *       Mapping rules
    1174                 :            :  *       -------------
    1175                 :            :  *       - 'file' protocol: each location (URI of local file) gets mapped to one
    1176                 :            :  *                                              and one only primary segdb.
    1177                 :            :  *       - 'http' protocol: each location (URI of http server) gets mapped to one
    1178                 :            :  *                                              and one only primary segdb.
    1179                 :            :  *       - 'gpfdist' and 'gpfdists' protocols: all locations (URI of gpfdist(s) client) are mapped
    1180                 :            :  *                                              to all primary segdbs. If there are less URIs than
    1181                 :            :  *                                              segdbs (usually the case) the URIs are duplicated
    1182                 :            :  *                                              so that there will be one for each segdb. However, if
    1183                 :            :  *                                              the GUC variable gp_external_max_segs is set to a num
    1184                 :            :  *                                              less than (total segdbs/total URIs) then we make sure
    1185                 :            :  *                                              that no URI gets mapped to more than this GUC number by
    1186                 :            :  *                                              skipping some segdbs randomly.
    1187                 :            :  *       - 'gphdfs' protocol: file is divided in to chucks and each chuck is assigned
    1188                 :            :  *                                              to a segdb.
    1189                 :            :  *       - 'exec' protocol: all segdbs get mapped to execute the command (this is
    1190                 :            :  *                                              soon to be changed though).
    1191                 :            :  */
    1192                 :            : static ExternalScan *

    1320                 :            :         /*
    1321                 :            :          * Now we do the actual assignment of work to the segment databases (where
    1322                 :            :          * work is either a URI to open or a command to execute). Due to the big
    1323                 :            :          * differences between the different protocols we handle each one
    1324                 :            :          * separately. Unfortunately this means some code duplication, but keeping
    1325                 :            :          * this separation makes the code much more understandable and (even) more
    1326                 :            :          * maintainable.
    1327                 :            :          *
    1328                 :            :          * Outline of the following code blocks (from simplest to most complex):
    1329                 :            :          * (only one of these will get executed for a statement)
    1330                 :            :          *
    1331                 :            :          * 1) segment mapping for tables with LOCATION http:// or file:// .
    1332                 :            :          *
    1333                 :            :          * These two protocols are very similar in that they enforce a
    1334                 :            :          * 1-URI:1-segdb relationship. The only difference between them is that
    1335                 :            :          * file:// URI must be assigned to a segdb on a host that is local to that
    1336                 :            :          * URI.
    1337                 :            :          *
    1338                 :            :          * 2) segment mapping for tables with LOCATION gpfdist(s):// or custom
    1339                 :            :          * protocol
    1340                 :            :          *
    1341                 :            :          * This protocol is more complicated - in here we usually duplicate the
    1342                 :            :          * user supplied gpfdist(s):// URIs until there is one available to every
    1343                 :            :          * segdb. However, in some cases (as determined by gp_external_max_segs
    1344                 :            :          * GUC) we don't want to use *all* segdbs but instead figure out how many
    1345                 :            :          * and pick them randomly (this is mainly for better performance and
    1346                 :            :          * resource mgmt).
    1347                 :            :          *
    1348                 :            :          * 3) segment mapping for tables with EXECUTE 'cmd' ON.
    1349                 :            :          *
    1350                 :            :          * In here we don't have URI's. We have a single command string and a
    1351                 :            :          * specification of the segdb granularity it should get executed on (the
    1352                 :            :          * ON clause). Depending on the ON clause specification we could go many
    1353                 :            :          * different ways, for example: assign the command to all segdb, or one
    1354                 :            :          * command per host, or assign to 5 random segments, etc...
    1355                 :            :          *
    1356                 :            :          * 4) segment mapping for tables with LOCATION gphdfs://
    1357                 :            :          *
    1358                 :            :          * The file chuck division and assignment will be done in the external
    1359                 :            :          * Java program. We simply assign the location to all the segdbs.
    1360                 :            :          */
    1361                 :            :

    3403                 :            :  *        index's attribute number, not the attribute number in the original rel.
    3404                 :            :  *      * If the index key is on the right, commute the clause to put it on the
    3405                 :            :  *        left.
    3406                 :            :  *      * We must construct lists of operator strategy numbers and subtypes
    3407                 :            :  *        for the top-level operators of each index clause.
    3408                 :            :  *      * We must detect any lossy index operators.  The API is that we return
    3409                 :            :  *        a list of the input clauses whose operators are NOT lossy.
    3410                 :            :  *
    3411                 :            :  * fixed_indexquals receives a modified copy of the indexquals list --- the
    3412                 :            :  * original is not changed.  Note also that the copy shares no substructure
    3413                 :            :  * with the original; this is needed in case there is a subplan in it (we need
    3414                 :            :  * two separate copies of the subplan tree, or things will go awry).
    3415                 :            :  *
    3416                 :            :  * nonlossy_indexquals receives a list of the original input clauses (with

    3419                 :            :  * indexstrategy receives an integer list of strategy numbers.
    3420                 :            :  * indexsubtype receives an OID list of strategy subtypes.

    3591                 :            : static Node *
    3592                 :            : fix_indexqual_operand(Node *node, IndexOptInfo *index, Oid *opfamily)
    3593                 :            : {
    3594                 :            :         /*
    3595                 :            :          * We represent index keys by Var nodes having the varno of the base table
    3596                 :            :          * but varattno equal to the index's attribute number (index column
    3597                 :            :          * position).  This is a bit hokey ... would be cleaner to use a
    3598                 :            :          * special-purpose node type that could not be mistaken for a regular Var.
    3599                 :            :          * But it will do for now.
    3600                 :            :          */

    3602                 :            :         int                     pos;
    3603                 :            :         ListCell   *indexpr_item;

    3618                 :            :                 {

    3624                 :          0 :                                         result->varattno = pos + 1;
    3625                 :            :                                         /* return the correct opfamily, too */
    3626                 :          0 :                                         *opfamily = index->opfamily[pos];
    3627                 :          0 :                                         return (Node *) result;
    3628                 :            :                                 }
    3629                 :          0 :                         }
    3630                 :          0 :                 }
    3631                 :          0 :         }
    3632                 :            :

    3634                 :          0 :         indexpr_item = list_head(index->indexprs);

    3666                 :            : /*
    3667                 :            :  * get_switched_clauses
    3668                 :            :  *        Given a list of merge or hash joinclauses (as RestrictInfo nodes),
    3669                 :            :  *        extract the bare clauses, and rearrange the elements within the
    3670                 :            :  *        clauses, if needed, so the outer join variable is on the left and
    3671                 :            :  *        the inner is on the right.  The original clause data structure is not
    3672                 :            :  *        touched; a modified list is returned.  We do, however, set the transient
    3673                 :            :  *        outer_is_left field in each RestrictInfo to show which side was which.

    3731                 :            : 
    3732                 :            : /*
    3733                 :            :  * order_qual_clauses
    3734                 :            :  *              Given a list of qual clauses that will all be evaluated at the same
    3735                 :            :  *              plan node, sort the list into the order we want to check the quals
    3736                 :            :  *              in at runtime.
    3737                 :            :  *
    3738                 :            :  * Ideally the order should be driven by a combination of execution cost and
    3739                 :            :  * selectivity, but it's not immediately clear how to account for both,
    3740                 :            :  * and given the uncertainty of the estimates the reliability of the decisions
    3741                 :            :  * would be doubtful anyway.  So we just order by estimated per-tuple cost,
    3742                 :            :  * being careful not to change the order when (as is often the case) the
    3743                 :            :  * estimates are identical.
    3744                 :            :  *
    3745                 :            :  * Although this will work on either bare clauses or RestrictInfos, it's
    3746                 :            :  * much faster to apply it to RestrictInfos, since it can re-use cost
    3747                 :            :  * information that is cached in RestrictInfos.
    3748                 :            :  *
    3749                 :            :  * Note: some callers pass lists that contain entries that will later be
    3750                 :            :  * removed; this is the easiest way to let this routine see RestrictInfos
    3751                 :            :  * instead of bare clauses.  It's OK because we only sort by cost, but
    3752                 :            :  * a cost/selectivity combination would likely do the wrong thing.
    3753                 :            :  */
    3754                 :            : static List *
    3755                 :            : order_qual_clauses(PlannerInfo *root, List *clauses)
    3756                 :            : {
    3757                 :            :         typedef struct
    3758                 :            :         {
    3759                 :            :                 Node       *clause;
    3760                 :            :                 Cost            cost;
    3761                 :            :         } QualItem;
    3762                 :          0 :         int                     nitems = list_length(clauses);
    3763                 :            :         QualItem   *items;
    3764                 :            :         ListCell   *lc;
    3765                 :            :         int                     i;
    3766                 :            :         List       *result;
    3767                 :            : 
    3768                 :            :         /* No need to work hard for 0 or 1 clause */
    3769         [ #  # ]:          0 :         if (nitems <= 1)
    3770                 :          0 :                 return clauses;
    3771                 :            : 
    3772                 :            :         /*
    3773                 :            :          * Collect the items and costs into an array.  This is to avoid repeated
    3774                 :            :          * cost_qual_eval work if the inputs aren't RestrictInfos.
    3775                 :            :          */
    3776                 :          0 :         items = (QualItem *) palloc(nitems * sizeof(QualItem));
    3777                 :          0 :         i = 0;
    3778         [ #  # ]:          0 :         foreach(lc, clauses)
    3779                 :            :         {
    3780                 :          0 :                 Node       *clause = (Node *) lfirst(lc);
    3781                 :            :                 QualCost        qcost;
    3782                 :            : 
    3783                 :          0 :                 cost_qual_eval_node(&qcost, clause, root);
    3784                 :          0 :                 items[i].clause = clause;
    3785                 :          0 :                 items[i].cost = qcost.per_tuple;
    3786                 :          0 :                 i++;
    3787                 :          0 :         }
    3788                 :            : 
    3789                 :            :         /*
    3790                 :            :          * Sort.  We don't use qsort() because it's not guaranteed stable for
    3791                 :            :          * equal keys.  The expected number of entries is small enough that a
    3792                 :            :          * simple insertion sort should be good enough.
    3793                 :            :          */
    3794         [ #  # ]:          0 :         for (i = 1; i < nitems; i++)
    3795                 :            :         {
    3796                 :          0 :                 QualItem        newitem = items[i];
    3797                 :            :                 int                     j;
    3798                 :            : 
    3799                 :            :                 /* insert newitem into the already-sorted subarray */
    3800         [ #  # ]:          0 :                 for (j = i; j > 0; j--)
    3801                 :            :                 {
    3802         [ #  # ]:          0 :                         if (newitem.cost >= items[j - 1].cost)
    3803                 :          0 :                                 break;
    3804                 :          0 :                         items[j] = items[j - 1];
    3805                 :          0 :                 }
    3806                 :          0 :                 items[j] = newitem;
    3807                 :          0 :         }
    3808                 :            : 
    3809                 :            :         /* Convert back to a list */
    3810                 :          0 :         result = NIL;
    3811         [ #  # ]:          0 :         for (i = 0; i < nitems; i++)
    3812                 :          0 :                 result = lappend(result, items[i].clause);
    3813                 :            : 
    3814                 :          0 :         return result;
    3815                 :          0 : }
    3816                 :            : 
    3817                 :            : /*
    3818                 :            :  * Copy cost and size info from a Path node to the Plan node created from it.
    3819                 :            :  * The executor won't use this info, but it's needed by EXPLAIN.
    3820                 :            :  */
    3821                 :            : static void
    3822                 :            : copy_path_costsize(PlannerInfo *root, Plan *dest, Path *src)
    3823                 :            : {
    3824         [ #  # ]:          0 :         if (src)
    3825                 :            :         {
    3826                 :          0 :                 dest->startup_cost = src->startup_cost;
    3827                 :          0 :                 dest->total_cost = src->total_cost;
    3828                 :          0 :                 dest->plan_rows = cdbpath_rows(root, src);
    3829                 :          0 :                 dest->plan_width = src->parent->width;
    3830                 :          0 :         }
    3831                 :            :         else

    5148                 :            :     /* Solution for MPP-11942
    5149                 :            :      * Before this fix, we calculated the width from the sub_tlist which
    5150                 :            :      * only contains a subset of the tlist. For example, for the query
    5151                 :            :      * select a, min(b), max(b), min(c), max(c) from s group by a;
    5152                 :            :      * the sub_tlist has the columns {a,b,c} while the tlist
    5153                 :            :      * is {a, min(b), max(b), min(c), max(c)}. Therefore, the plan_width
    5154                 :            :      * for the above query is calculated to be 12 instead of 20.
    5155                 :            :      *
    5156                 :            :      * In this fix, we calculate the actual row width from the tlist.
    5157                 :            :      */
    5158                 :            : 
    5159                 :          0 :     plan->plan_width = get_row_width(tlist);
    5160                 :            : 
    5161         [ #  # ]:          0 :         if (aggstrategy == AGG_HASHED)
    5162                 :            :         {
    5163                 :            :                 /* The following estimate is very rough but good enough for planning. */
    5164                 :          0 :                 entrywidth = agg_hash_entrywidth(numAggs,
    5165                 :          0 :                                                                    sizeof(HeapTupleData) + sizeof(HeapTupleHeaderData) + plan->plan_width,
    5166                 :          0 :                                                                    transSpace);
    5167 [ #  # ][ #  # ]:          0 :                 if (!calcHashAggTableSizes(global_work_mem(root),
